The interface may also provide the ability to create or modify existing records.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e"]]],[null,null,null,null,null,null,null,null,[[[null,"\u003cp\u003eFigure 5: Default Record List view for Account object\u003c/p\u003e"],["https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/aurainspector-fig5.max-900x900.png",null,null,"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/aurainspector-fig5.max-900x900.png"],null,3]]],[null,null,[null,[null,"\u003ch4\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eHome URLs\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eHome URLs are URLs that can be browsed to directly. On multiple occasions, following these URLs led Mandiant researchers to administration or configuration panels for third-party modules installed on the Salesforce instance. They can be retrieved by authenticated users with the \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eui.communities.components.aura.components.communitySetup.cmc.\u003cbr\u003eCMCAppController/ACTION$getAppBootstrapData\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e Aura method as follows:\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e"]]],[null,null,[null,[null,"\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode\u003e{\"actions\":[{\"id\":\"1086;a\",\"descriptor\":\"serviceComponent://ui.communities.components.aura.components.communitySetup.cmc.CMCAppController/ACTION$getAppBootstrapData\",\"callingDescriptor\":\"UNKNOWN\",\"params\":{}}]}\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e"]]],[null,null,[null,[null,"\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eIn the returned JSON response, an object named \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eapiNameToObjectHomeUrls\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e contains the list of URLs. The next step is to browse to each URL, verify access, and assess whether the content should be accessible. It is a straightforward process that can lead to interesting findings. An example of usage is shown in Figure 6.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e"]]],[null,null,null,null,null,null,null,null,[[[null,"\u003cp\u003eFigure 6: List of home URLs returned in response\u003c/p\u003e"],["https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/aurainspector-fig6.max-800x800.png",null,null,"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/aurainspector-fig6.max-800x800.png"],null,3]]],[null,null,[null,[null,"\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eDuring a previous engagement, Mandiant identified a Spark instance administration dashboard accessible to any unauthenticated user via this method. The dashboard offered administrative features, as seen in Figure 7.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e"]]],[null,null,null,null,null,null,null,null,[[[null,"\u003cp\u003eFigure 7: Spark instance administration dashboard\u003c/p\u003e"],["https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/aurainspector-fig7.max-900x900.png",null,null,"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/aurainspector-fig7.max-900x900.png"],null,3]]],[null,null,[null,[null,"\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eUsing this technique, Salesforce administrators can identify pages that should not be accessible to unauthenticated or low-privilege users. Manually tracking down these pages can be cumbersome as some pages are automatically created when installing marketplace applications.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch4\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eSelf-Registration\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eOver the last few years, \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href\u003d\"https://help.salesforce.com/s/articleView?id\u003dplatform.networks_guest_policies_timelines.htm\u0026amp;type\u003d5\" rel\u003d\"noopener\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eSalesforce has increased the default security on Guest accounts\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e. As such, having an authenticated account is even more valuable as it might give access to records not accessible to unauthenticated users. One solution to prevent authenticated access to the instance is to prevent self-registration. Self-registration can easily be disabled by changing the instance's settings. However, Mandiant observed cases where the link to the self-registration page was removed from the login page, but self-registration itself was not disabled. Salesforce confirmed this issue has been resolved.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eAura methods that expose the self-registration status and URL are highly valuable from an adversary's perspective. The \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003egetIsSelfRegistrationEnabled\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e and \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003egetSelfRegistrationUrl\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e methods of the \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eLoginFormController\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e controller can be used as follows to retrieve this information:\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e"]]],[null,null,[null,[null,"\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode\u003e{\"actions\":[{\"id\":\"1\",\"descriptor\":\"apex://applauncher.LoginFormController/ACTION$getIsSelfRegistrationEnabled\",\"callingDescriptor\":\"UHNKNOWN\"},{\"id\":\"2\",\"descriptor\":\"apex://applauncher.LoginFormController/ACTION$getSelfRegistrationUrl\",\"callingDescriptor\":\"UHNKNOWN\"}]}\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e"]]],[null,null,[null,[null,"\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eBy bulking the two methods, two responses are returned from the server. In Figure 8, self-registration is available as shown in the first response, and the URL is returned in the second response.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e"]]],[null,null,null,null,null,null,null,null,[[[null,"\u003cp\u003eFigure 8: Response when self-registration is enabled\u003c/p\u003e"],["https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/aurainspector-fig8.max-1000x1000.png",null,null,"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/aurainspector-fig8.max-1000x1000.png"],null,3]]],[null,null,[null,[null,"\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eThis removes the need to perform brute forcing to identify the self-registration page; one request is sufficient. The \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href\u003d\"https://github.com/google/aura-inspector\" rel\u003d\"noopener\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eAuraInspector\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e tool verifies whether self-registration is enabled and alerts the researcher. The goal is to help Salesforce administrators determine whether self-registration is enabled or not from an external perspective.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eGraphQL: Going Beyond the 2,000 Records Limit\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eSalesforce provides a GraphQL API that can be used to easily retrieve records from objects that are accessible via the User Interface API from the Salesforce instance. The GraphQL API itself is well documented by Salesforce. However, there is no official documentation or research related to the GraphQL Aura controller.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e"]]],[null,null,null,null,null,null,null,null,[[[null,"\u003cp\u003eFigure 9: GraphQL query from the documentation\u003c/p\u003e"],["https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/aurainspector-fig9.max-900x900.png",null,null,"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/aurainspector-fig9.max-900x900.png"],null,3]]],[null,null,[null,[null,"\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eThis lack of documentation, however, does not prevent its use. After reviewing the REST API documentation, Mandiant constructed a valid request to retrieve information for the GraphQL Aura controller. Furthermore, this controller was available to unauthenticated users by default. Using GraphQL over the known methods offers multiple advantages:\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli style\u003d\"list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eStandardized retrieval of records and information about objects\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli style\u003d\"list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eImproved pagination, allowing for the retrieval of all records tied to an object\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli style\u003d\"list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eBuilt-in introspection, which facilitates the retrieval of field names\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli style\u003d\"list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eSupport for mutations, which expedites the testing of write privileges on objects\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eFrom a data retrieval perspective, the key advantage is the ability to retrieve all records tied to an object without being limited to 2,000 records. Salesforce confirmed this is not a vulnerability; GraphQL respects the underlying object permissions and does not provide additional access as long as access to objects is properly configured. However, in the case of a misconfiguration, it helps attackers access any amount of records on the misconfigured objects. When using basic Aura controllers to retrieve records, the only way to retrieve more than 2,000 records is by using sorting filters, which does not always provide consistent results. Using the GraphQL controller enables the consistent retrieval of the maximum number of records possible. Other options to retrieve more than 2,000 records are the SOAP and REST APIs, but those are rarely accessible to non-privileged users.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eOne limitation of the GraphQL Controller is that it can only retrieve records for User Interface API (UIAPI) supported objects. As explained in the associated Salesforce \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href\u003d\"https://developer.salesforce.com/docs/atlas.en-us.uiapi.meta/uiapi/ui_api_get_started_supported_objects.htm\" rel\u003d\"noopener\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eGraphQL API documentation\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e, this encompasses most objects as the \"User Interface API supports all custom objects and external objects and many standard objects.\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eSince there is no documentation on the GraphQL Aura controller itself, the API documentation was used as a reference. The API documentation provides the following example to interact with the GraphQL API endpoint:\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e"]]],[null,null,[null,[null,"\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode\u003ecurl \"https://{MyDomainName}[.my.salesforce.com/services/data/v64.0/graphql](https://.my.salesforce.com/services/data/v64.0/graphql)\" \\\r\n  -X POST \\\r\n  -H \"content-type: application/json\" \\\r\n  -d '{\r\n  \"query\": \"query accounts { uiapi { query { Account { edges { node { Name { value } } } } } } }\"\r\n}\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e"]]],[null,null,[null,[null,"\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eThis example was then transposed to the GraphQL Aura controller. The following Aura message was found to work:\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e"]]],[null,null,[null,[null,"\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode\u003e{\"actions\":[{\"id\":\"GraphQL\",\"descriptor\":\"aura://RecordUiController/ACTION$executeGraphQL\",\"callingDescriptor\":\"markup://forceCommunity:richText\",\"params\":{\"queryInput\":{\"operationName\":\"accounts\",\"query\":\"query+accounts+{uiapi+{query+{Account+{edges+{node+{+Name+{+value+}}}totalCount,pageInfo{endCursor,hasNextPage,hasPreviousPage}}}}}\",\"variables\":{}}},\"version\":\"64.0\",\"storable\":true}]}\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e"]]],[null,null,[null,[null,"\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eThis provides the same capabilities as the GraphQL API without requiring API access. The \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eendCursor\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e, \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003ehasNextPage\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e, and \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003ehasPreviousPage\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e fields were added in the response to facilitate pagination. The requests and response can be seen in Figure 10.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e"]]],[null,null,null,null,null,null,null,null,[[[null,"\u003cp\u003eFigure 10: Response when using the GraphQL Aura Controller\u003c/p\u003e"],["https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/aurainspector-fig10.max-1200x1200.png","https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/aurainspector-fig10.max-1100x1100.png 1060w, https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/aurainspector-fig10.max-1200x1200.png 1118w"," 1060px,  1118px","https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/aurainspector-fig10.max-1200x1200.png"],null,3]]],[null,null,[null,[null,"\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eThe records would be returned with the fields queried and a \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003epageInfo\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e object containing the cursor. Using the cursor, it is possible to retrieve the next records. In the aforementioned example, only one record was retrieved for readability, but this can be done in batches of 2,000 records by setting the \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003efirst\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e parameter to \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e2000\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e. The cursor can then be used as shown in Figure 11.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e"]]],[null,null,null,null,null,null,null,null,[[[null,"\u003cp\u003eFigure 11: Retrieving next records using the cursor\u003c/p\u003e"],["https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/aurainspector-fig11.max-900x900.png","https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/aurainspector-fig11.max-900x900.png 859w, https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/aurainspector-fig11.max-900x900.png 859w"," 859px,  859px","https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/aurainspector-fig11.max-900x900.png"],null,3]]],[null,null,[null,[null,"\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eHere, the cursor is a Base64-encoded string indicating the latest record retrieved, so it can easily be built from scratch. With batches of 2,000 records, and to retrieve the items from 2,000 to 4,000, the message would be:\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e"]]],[null,null,[null,[null,"\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode\u003emessage\u003d{\"actions\":[{\"id\":\"GraphQL\",\"descriptor\":\"aura://RecordUiController/ACTION$executeGraphQL\",\"callingDescriptor\":\"markup://forceCommunity:richText\",\"params\":{\"queryInput\":{\"operationName\":\"accounts\",\"query\":\"query+accounts+{uiapi+{query+{Contact(first:2000,after:\\\"djE6MTk5OQ\u003d\u003d\\\"){edges+{node+{+Name+{+value+}}}totalCount,pageInfo{endCursor,hasNextPage,hasPreviousPage}}}}}\",\"variables\":{}}},\"version\":\"64.0\",\"storable\":true}]}\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e"]]],[null,null,[null,[null,"\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eIn the example, the cursor, set in the \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eafter\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e parameter, is the base64 for \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003ev1:1999\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e. It tells Salesforce to retrieve items after \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e1999\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e. Queries can be much more complex, involving advanced filtering or join operations to search for specific records. Multiple objects can also be retrieved in one query. Though not covered in detail here, the GraphQL controller can also be used to update, create, and delete records by using mutation queries. This allows unauthenticated users to perform complex queries and operations without requiring API access.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eRemediation\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eAll of the issues described in this blogpost stem from misconfigurations, specifically on objects and fields. At a high level, Salesforce administrators should take the following steps to remediate these issues:\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli style\u003d\"list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eAudit Guest User Permissions:\u003c/strong\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e Regularly review and apply the principle of least privilege to unauthenticated \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href\u003d\"https://help.salesforce.com/s/articleView?id\u003dplatform.rss_config_guest_user_profile.htm\u0026amp;language\u003den_US\u0026amp;type\u003d5\" rel\u003d\"noopener\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eguest user profiles\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e. Follow Salesforce security \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href\u003d\"https://help.salesforce.com/s/articleView?id\u003dplatform.networks_object_specific_best_practices.htm\u0026amp;type\u003d5\" rel\u003d\"noopener\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003ebest practices\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e for guest users object security. Ensure they only have read access to the specific objects and fields necessary for public-facing functionality.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli style\u003d\"list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eSecure Private Data for Authenticated Users:\u003c/strong\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e Review \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href\u003d\"https://help.salesforce.com/s/articleView?id\u003dplatform.security_sharing_rules_edit.htm\u0026amp;type\u003d5\" rel\u003d\"noopener\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003esharing rules\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e and \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href\u003d\"https://help.salesforce.com/s/articleView?id\u003dplatform.security_sharing_owd_about.htm\u0026amp;language\u003den_US\u0026amp;type\u003d5\" rel\u003d\"noopener\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eorganization-wide defaults\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan to.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli style\u003d\"list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong
